## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Population Ecology / Mathematical Biology
**Analysis**: This task models the instantaneous population growth rate as a function of current population size and time, which is fundamental to mathematical biology and theoretical ecology. The relationships typically capture intrinsic reproduction, density-dependent feedback, environmental fluctuations, and critical thresholds like carrying capacity or Allee effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resource growth regime)
- Gompertz growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (growth rate proportional to log of remaining capacity)
- Theta-logistic regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (generalized density-dependent feedback)
- Ricker-type competition: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong overcompensatory density dependence)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (critical threshold below which population declines)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental modulation)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * t)) (gradual environmental degradation or improvement)
- Beverton-Holt type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (smooth transition from exponential to zero growth)
- Logarithmic stress feedback: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * log(P)) (physiological constraint scaling with population)
- Harvesting-adjusted dynamics: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * t (external extraction rate increasing over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent feedback → Linear (1 - c*P), polynomial, or exponential exp(-c*P) damping terms that reduce growth rate as P increases
- Allee threshold behavior → Growth rate crosses zero at positive P, structurally modeled by (P - c1) factors multiplying the base rate
- Seasonal/periodic modulation → Trigonometric terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) scaling the intrinsic reproduction rate to capture environmental cycles
- Time-dependent environmental shift → Explicit t dependence in coefficients like c0 * (1 + c1 * t) or exp(c2 * t) representing gradual habitat change
- Overcompensatory competition → Non-linear decay exp(-c*P) or high-degree polynomials causing sharp growth suppression at high densities
- Asymptotic saturation → Growth rate approaches zero as P increases, enforced by (c - P) factors or rational denominators (1 + c*P)
- External mortality/harvesting → Subtractive terms c0 - c1 * t or c0 - c1 * P representing constant or density-proportional removal
- Logarithmic feedback regulation → Terms like log(P) or P * log(P) capturing slowing growth due to physiological stress or resource scarcity

$-P + P^2/C + P^2/B - P^3/(BC)$
Multiply by $A$:
$-A P + A P^2/C + A P^2/B - A P^3/(BC)$
Add the remaining terms $A P^{1/3} + A P$:
GT = $-A P + A P^2/C + A P^2/B - A P^3/(BC) + A P^{1/3} + A P$
The $-A P$ and $+ A P$ cancel out!
So GT simplifies to:
GT = $A P^{1/3} + A P^2 (1/C + 1/B) - A P^3 / (BC)$
Let's check the coefficients:
$A = 0.8677806610632854$
$1/C + 1/B = 1/14.185052779605893 + 1/6.057935627201261 \approx 0.070496 + 0.165073 = 0.235569$
$1/(BC) = 1/(14.185052779605893 * 6.057935627201261) \approx 1/85.933 \approx 0.011637$
So GT is essentially a polynomial in $P$ of degree 3, plus a $P^{1/3}$ term.
Specifically: GT = $c_a P^{1/3} + c_b P^2 + c_c P^3$
Wait, let's re-evaluate carefully.
GT = $c_0 (-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4) P + c_5 P^{c_6} + c_7 P$
With given values: $c_0 = c_5 = c_7 = A$, $c_1 = 1$, $c_3 = 1$, $c_6 = 1/3$.
So GT = $A (-1 + P/c_2)(1 - P/c_4) P + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= A P [ (-1)(1) + (-1)(-P/c_4) + (P/c_2)(1) + (P/c_2)(-P/c_4) ] + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= A P [ -1 + P/c_4 + P/c_2 - P^2/(c_2 c_4) ] + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= -A P + A P^2/c_4 + A P^2/c_2 - A P^3/(c_2 c_4) + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= A P^{1/3} + A (1/c_2 + 1/c_4) P^2 - A/(c_2 c_4) P^3$
So the GT is exactly of the form: $k_1 P^{1/3} + k_2 P^2 + k_3 P^3$.
There is no constant term, no $P^1$ term, no $P^4$ term, no exponentials, no logs, no trig functions.
It's a simple combination of $P^{1/3}$, $P^2$, and $P^3$.

Let's check the candidates. Many candidates have complex structures with denominators like $(P*c1 + 1)$, exponentials, logs, etc.
If a candidate has a denominator that depends on $P$, it can only match a polynomial if the denominator divides the numerator exactly, or if the denominator is a constant. But here denominators are like $(P*c1+1)$, which is not constant. So candidates with such denominators are likely NO MATCH, unless the numerator has a factor that cancels it out, or the extra terms are zeroed out. But the structure of the numerator in these candidates usually doesn't have $(P*c1+1)$ as a factor for all terms.
Wait, let's look at Candidate 15:
`(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P**2*c2*(P*c1 + 1) + P**2*(-P**2 + P*c3 + 1))/(P*c1 + 1)`
Divide term by term:
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P^2 + \frac{P^2(-P^2 + P c_3 + 1)}{P c_1 + 1}$
The last term is a rational function, not a polynomial, unless $P c_1 + 1$ divides $-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2$. This is generally not true for arbitrary $c_1$. So NO MATCH.

Let's look for candidates that are simply sums of $P^{1/3}$, $P^2$, $P^3$.
Candidate 16: `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3)`
$= c_0 P^3 + c_1 P^2 + c_3 P^{c_2+1}$
If we set $c_2 = -2/3$, then $P^{c_2+1} = P^{1/3}$.
So Candidate 16 can be $c_0 P^3 + c_1 P^2 + c_3 P^{1/3}$.
This matches the form of GT exactly!
Let's verify: GT = $k_1 P^{1/3} + k_2 P^2 + k_3 P^3$.
Candidate 16: $c_3 P^{c_2+1} + c_1 P^2 + c_0 P^3$.
We can set $c_2 = 1/3 - 1 = -2/3$. Then $c_2+1 = 1/3$.
So Candidate 16 matches.

Candidate 17: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1 + c2*Abs(P)**3`
Since $P \ge 0$, $|P|^3 = P^3$.
So this is $c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P^2 + c_2 P^3$. Matches exactly.

Candidate 18: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2`
Matches exactly.

Candidate 19: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*(P*c1 + c2)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P^3 + c_2 P^2$. Matches exactly.

Candidate 6: `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P**c3*c4 + 1) + c5)`
$= c_0 P^3 + c_1 P^2 + c_2 c_4 P^{c_3+1} + c_2 P + c_5 P$.
We need $P^{1/3}$ term. So $c_3+1 = 1/3 \Rightarrow c_3 = -2/3$.
Then we have extra terms $c_2 P + c_5 P = (c_2+c_5) P$.
We can set $c_2 = 0$ and $c_5 = 0$ to eliminate the $P$ term.
Then it becomes $c_0 P^3 + c_1 P^2$. But we lose the $P^{1/3}$ term because $c_2 c_4 = 0$.
Wait, if $c_2=0$, the $P^{1/3}$ term vanishes. So we can't get $P^{1/3}$ without getting a $P$ term, unless $c_2 \neq 0$ but we can't cancel $P$ term independently? Actually, the term is $c_2(P^{c_3} c_4 + 1)$. If $c_3 = -2/3$, it's $c_2(c_4 P^{-2/3} + 1)$. Multiplied by $P$ gives $c_2 c_4 P^{1/3} + c_2 P$.
We need to eliminate $c_2 P$. We can't, because $c_2$ is shared. Unless $c_2=0$, but then $P^{1/3}$ is gone.
So Candidate 6 is NO MATCH.

Candidate 7: `P*(c0 + c1*(P + c2)*(P + c3) + c4*(P**c5*c6 + 1))`
$= c_0 P + c_1 P(P^2 + (c_2+c_3)P + c_2 c_3) + c_4 c_6 P^{c_5+1} + c_4 P$
$= c_1 P^3 + c_1(c_2+c_3) P^2 + (c_0 + c_1 c_2 c_3 + c_4) P + c_4 c_6 P^{c_5+1}$.
We need $P^{1/3}$, so $c_5 = -2/3$.
We have a $P$ term with coefficient $(c_0 + c_1 c_2 c_3 + c_4)$. We can set this to 0.
So we can match $c_1 P^3 + c_1(c_2+c_3) P^2 + c_4 c_6 P^{1/3}$.
This matches the form! So Candidate 7 is a MATCH.

Candidate 11: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2 + 1)**2 + P*(P*c3 + c4)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P (c_2^2 P^2 + 2 c_2 P + 1) + c_3 P^2 + c_4 P$
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 c_2^2 P^3 + (2 c_1 c_2 + c_3) P^2 + (c_1 + c_4) P$.
We can set $c_1 + c_4 = 0$ to eliminate $P$.
Then we have $c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 c_2^2 P^3 + (2 c_1 c_2 + c_3) P^2$. Matches form. So MATCH.

Candidate 12: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P + c2)*(P + c3) + P*(P*c4 + c5)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P(P^2 + (c_2+c_3)P + c_2 c_3) + c_4 P^2 + c_5 P$
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P^3 + (c_1(c_2+c_3) + c_4) P^2 + (c_1 c_2 c_3 + c_5) P$.
Set $c_1 c_2 c_3 + c_5 = 0$. Matches form. So MATCH.

Candidate 13: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P**2*c2 + 1) + P*(P*c3 + c4)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 c_2 P^3 + c_1 P + c_3 P^2 + c_4 P$
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 c_2 P^3 + c_3 P^2 + (c_1 + c_4) P$.
Set $c_1 + c_4 = 0$. Matches form. So MATCH.

Candidate 14: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*(P + c3)*(P + c4)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P + c_2 P(P^2 + (c_3+c_4)P + c_3 c_4)$
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P^3 + c_2(c_3+c_4) P^2 + (c_1 + c_2 c_3 c_4) P$.
Set $c_1 + c_2 c_3 c_4 = 0$. Matches form. So MATCH.

Candidate 28: `sqrt(P)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4 + c5 + c6*exp(P*c7) + c8*exp(P*c7)/P + c9/sqrt(P)`
Has $\sqrt{P}$, $e^P$, $1/P$, etc. Cannot match polynomial + $P^{1/3}$. NO MATCH.

Candidate 50: `P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + c3*log(P*c4 + 1) + c5 + c6*log(c7*(P*c8 + c9) + 1)`
Has logs. NO MATCH.

Now let's check candidates with denominators. Sometimes they simplify.
Candidate 3: `(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P*c2*(P + c3)*(P + c4)*(P*c1 + 1) + P*(-P**3 + P**2*c5 + P + c6))/(P*c1 + 1)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P(P+c_3)(P+c_4) + \frac{P(-P^3 + c_5 P^2 + P + c_6)}{P c_1 + 1}$
The last term is rational. Unless $P c_1 + 1$ divides the numerator, it's not a polynomial. Generally NO MATCH.

Candidate 9: `(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P*c2*(P*c1 + 1) + P*(-P**3 + P**2*c3 + P + c4))/(P*c1 + 1)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P + \frac{P(-P^3 + c_3 P^2 + P + c_4)}{P c_1 + 1}$. Rational term. NO MATCH.

Candidate 10: `(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P*c2*exp(P*c3) + P*(-P**3 + P**2*c4 + P + c5))/(P*c1 + 1)`
Has exp. NO MATCH.

Candidate 20: `(P**(1/3)*c0*exp(P*c1) + c2*exp(P*c1) + c3 + (P**(1/3) + c4)*(P*(P**2*c5 + P*c6 + c7) + c8*log(P*c9 + 1)))/(P**(1/3) + c4)`
$= \frac{(P^{1/3}+c_4)(c_0 e^{P c_1} + \dots) + \dots}{P^{1/3}+c_4}$. Has exp and log. NO MATCH.

Candidate 21, 22, 32, 33, 35: Have $\sqrt{P}$. GT has $P^{1/3}$. $\sqrt{P} = P^{1/2} \neq P^{1/3}$. NO MATCH.

Candidate 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 30, 31, 37, 38, 39, 40, 41, 46: Have logs or exp or sin. NO MATCH.

Has log. NO MATCH.

Candidate 34, 36, 43, 44, 45, 47, 48, 49: Have exp or log. NO MATCH.

Has log and exp. NO MATCH.

So the matches are likely 6, 7, 11, 12, 13, 14, 16, 17, 18, 19.
Wait, I already ruled out 6. Let's re-verify 6.
Candidate 6: `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P**c3*c4 + 1) + c5)`
$= c_0 P^3 + c_1 P^2 + c_2 c_4 P^{c_3+1} + c_2 P + c_5 P$.
To get $P^{1/3}$, need $c_3 = -2/3$.

This matches the form $k_3 P^3 + k_2 P^2 + k_1 P^{1/3}$.

$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P(P^2 + (c_2+c_3)P + c_2 c_3) + c_4 P^2 + c_5 P$

Set $c_5 = -c_1 c_2 c_3$. Matches.

Candidate 13: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P**2*c2 + 1) + P*(P*c3 + c4)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 c_2 P^3 + c_1 P + c_3 P^2 + c_4 P$

All these 10 candidates match the structure $A P^{1/3} + B P^2 + C P^3$.
The GT simplifies exactly to this structure.
Let's quickly re-verify GT simplification.
GT = $c_0(-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4)P + c_5 P^{c_6} + c_7 P$
Given values: $c_0=c_5=c_7=A$, $c_1=1, c_3=1, c_6=1/3$.
GT = $A(-1 + P/c_2)(1 - P/c_4)P + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= A P [ -1 + P/c_4 + P/c_2 - P^2/(c_2 c_4) ] + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= -A P + A(1/c_4 + 1/c_2) P^2 - A/(c_2 c_4) P^3 + A P^{1/3} + A P$
$= A P^{1/3} + A(1/c_2 + 1/c_4) P^2 - A/(c_2 c_4) P^3$.
Yes, exactly $k_1 P^{1/3} + k_2 P^2 + k_3 P^3$.
No constant, no $P^1$, no $P^4$, etc.
So any candidate that can be reduced to this form is a match.
Candidates 6, 7, 11, 12, 13, 14, 16, 17, 18, 19 all reduce to this form by setting some constants to specific values or relations.
Are there any constraints I missed? "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number (including 0) to candidate constants". So yes, we can set them to cancel unwanted terms.

Let's check Candidate 15 again just in case.
`(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P**2*c2*(P*c1 + 1) + P**2*(-P**2 + P*c3 + 1))/(P*c1 + 1)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P^2 + \frac{-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2}{P c_1 + 1}$.
For this to be a polynomial, $P c_1 + 1$ must divide $-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2$.
Polynomial division: $-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2$ divided by $c_1 P + 1$.
Root of divisor is $P = -1/c_1$.
Evaluate numerator at $P = -1/c_1$: $-(-1/c_1)^4 + c_3(-1/c_1)^3 + (-1/c_1)^2 = -1/c_1^4 - c_3/c_1^3 + 1/c_1^2$.
For exact division, this must be 0.
$-1 - c_3 c_1 + c_1^2 = 0 \Rightarrow c_1^2 - c_1 c_3 - 1 = 0$.
This is a constraint on $c_1, c_3$. But even if it divides, the quotient will be a cubic polynomial.
Let's perform division assuming it divides:
$(-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2) / (c_1 P + 1) = -\frac{1}{c_1} P^3 + \frac{c_3 + 1/c_1}{c_1} P^2 + \dots$
It would yield a polynomial of degree 3. So it could potentially match.
But the condition $c_1^2 - c_1 c_3 - 1 = 0$ is a specific algebraic relation between constants. The prompt says "You can assign ANY real number ... to candidate constants". It doesn't say we can impose algebraic constraints between them unless they are free parameters. But here $c_1$ and $c_3$ are independent free parameters. We can choose $c_1=1, c_3=0$, then it doesn't divide. So it's not generally equivalent. It's only equivalent for a specific subset of parameter space. Thus, NO MATCH.

What about Candidate 3?
`(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P*c2*(P + c3)*(P + c4)*(P*c1 + 1) + P*(-P**3 + P**2*c5 + P + c6))/(P*c1 + 1)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P(P+c_3)(P+c_4) + \frac{-P^4 + c_5 P^3 + P^2 + c_6 P}{P c_1 + 1}$.
Same issue. Rational term. NO MATCH.

Candidate 9:
`(P**(1/3)*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + P*c2*(P*c1 + 1) + P*(-P**3 + P**2*c3 + P + c4))/(P*c1 + 1)`
$= c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P + \frac{-P^4 + c_3 P^3 + P^2 + c_4 P}{P c_1 + 1}$.
Rational term. NO MATCH.

So the list of matches remains: 6, 7, 11, 12, 13, 14, 16, 17, 18, 19.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6 + c7*P`
Substituting the given numerical values ($c_0=c_5=c_7 \approx 0.8678$, $c_1=c_3=1$, $c_6=1/3$):
`GT = A*(-1 + P/c2)*(1 - P/c4)*P + A*P**(1/3) + A*P`
Expanding the polynomial part:
`(-1 + P/c2)*(1 - P/c4)*P = (-1 + P/c4 + P/c2 - P^2/(c2*c4))*P = -P + (1/c4 + 1/c2)P^2 - P^3/(c2*c4)`
Multiplying by $A$ and adding the remaining terms:
`GT = -A*P + A*(1/c2 + 1/c4)*P^2 - A/(c2*c4)*P^3 + A*P**(1/3) + A*P`
The linear terms `-A*P` and `+A*P` cancel exactly. The GT simplifies to a strict combination of three basis functions:
`GT = k1 * P**(1/3) + k2 * P**2 + k3 * P**3`
where $k_1, k_2, k_3$ are non-zero constants. Any candidate must be algebraically reducible to this exact form (allowing free constants to cancel unwanted terms like $P^1$ or $P^4$).

### Candidate Verification
- **Candidates 1, 2, 4, 8, 10, 20, 26, 27, 30, 34, 37, 42, 43, 44, 47, 48, 49**: Contain `exp()` terms. Exponentials are linearly independent from polynomials and fractional powers. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidates 5, 23, 24, 25, 29, 31, 36, 38, 39, 40, 41, 45, 46, 50**: Contain `log()` terms. Logarithms cannot be exactly matched to polynomial/fractional power bases. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidates 21, 22, 28, 32, 33, 35**: Contain `sqrt(P)` ($P^{1/2}$). The GT requires $P^{1/3}$. Basis mismatch. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidates 3, 9, 15**: Contain rational structures with denominators like `(P*c1 + 1)`. These do not divide the numerators exactly for arbitrary constants, leaving irreducible rational terms or introducing $P^4$ terms when denominators are forced to 1. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 6**: `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P**c3*c4 + 1) + c5)` expands to `c0*P**3 + c1*P**2 + c2*c4*P**(c3+1) + (c2+c5)*P`. Setting `c3 = -2/3` yields `P**(1/3)`. Setting `c5 = -c2` eliminates the `P` term. Matches GT structure. `[MATCH]`

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

**GT expression:**
```
0.8678*(-1 + P/6.058)*(1 - P/14.185)*P + 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P
```

Let me expand the cubic part:
(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P²/(6.058×14.185)

So the first term becomes:
0.8678*P*[-1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P²/(6.058×14.185)]
= 0.8678*[-P + P²/14.185 + P²/6.058 - P³/(85.91)]

Combining: GT = 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P + 0.8678*(-P + aP² - bP³)
= 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P - 0.8678*P + 0.8678*(a)P² - 0.8678*bP³

Wait, let me be more careful:
= 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P + 0.8678*P*(-1 + P(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P²/(85.91))
= 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P - 0.8678*P + 0.8678*P²(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - 0.8678*P³/(85.91)

So GT = 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*(1/14.185 + 1/6.058)*P² - 0.8678/(85.91)*P³

**GT simplifies to: c_a*P^(1/3) + c_b*P² + c_c*P³**

where c_a, c_b, c_c are specific constants. The P terms cancel! Let me verify:
- From the expansion: +0.8678*P (from c7*P) and -0.8678*P (from the (-1)*P term in the product) → they cancel.

So **GT = A*P^(1/3) + B*P² + C*P³** where A > 0, B > 0, C < 0.

**Candidate 17:** P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + c2*|P|³

**Candidate 19:** P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*(c1*P + c2) = c0*P^(1/3) + c2*P² + c1*P³. ✓

**Candidate 13:** P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(c2*P² + 1) + P*(c3*P + c4) = c0*P^(1/3) + c1*c2*P³ + c1*P + c3*P² + c4*P. Has a P term that can't be zeroed without zeroing P³. Only if c1=0, but then P³ disappears. [NO MATCH]

Let me check candidates 12, 14, 11 similarly - they all have cross terms that force unwanted P terms.

**Candidate 16:** P*(c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2) - needs P^c2 = P^(-2/3) which gives P^(1/3). So c2 = -2/3: P³*c0 + P²*c1 + c3*P^(1/3). ✓

**Candidate 6:** P*(c0*P² + c1*P + c2*(c4*P^c3 + 1) + c5) = c0*P³ + c1*P² + c2*c4*P^(c3+1) + c2*P + c5*P. Need c3+1=1/3 → c3=-2/3, and c2+c5=0 to kill P term. But c2*P and c5*P: set c5 = -c2. Then: c0*P³ + c1*P² + c2*c4*P^(1/3). ✓

**Candidate 7:** Similar analysis - P*(c0 + c1*(P+c2)(P+c3) + c4*(c6*P^c5+1)). Expanding: c1*P³ + c1*(c2+c3)*P² + (c0+c1*c2*c3+c4)*P + c4*c6*P^(c5+1). Need c5=-2/3, and c0+c1*c2*c3+c4=0. ✓
